  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText13733439334273338608" style="display:none">In this sequel to the bestselling fantasy thriller, <i>Angelfall</i>, the survivors of the angel apocalypse begin to scrape back together what's left of the modern world.<br /><br />When a group of people capture Penryn's sister Paige, thinking she's a monster, the situation ends in a massacre. Paige disappears. Humans are terrified. Mom is heartbroken.<br /><br />Penryn drives through the streets of San Francisco looking for Paige. Why are the streets so empty? Where is everybody? Her search leads her into the heart of the angels' secret plans where she catches a glimpse of their motivations, and learns the horrifying extent to which the angels are willing to go.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Raffe hunts for his wings. Without them, he can't rejoin the angels, can't take his rightful place as one of their leaders. When faced with recapturing his wings or helping Penryn survive, which will he choose?</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3200571396587662458">This is me right now waiting for this sure-to-be-amazing book with a lot of my Goodreads friends:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681934.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I mean, come <i> on! </i> The first book was freaking amazing, and that last chapter.........that last freaking chapter. Damn. Can you all <i> imagine </i> what the second book is going to be like if the whole book is like that last chapter? Just think about it. I'd like to present you guys with..........<br/><br/><b> The Opening of the Second Book of Angelfall: A Tragic gif Play! </b> <br/><br/>Caitlin is walking down the road one day when</span>
  <span id="freeText3200571396587662458" style="display:none">This is me right now waiting for this sure-to-be-amazing book with a lot of my Goodreads friends:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681934.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, come <i> on! </i> The first book was freaking amazing, and that last chapter.........that last freaking chapter. Damn. Can you all <i> imagine </i> what the second book is going to be like if the whole book is like that last chapter? Just think about it. I'd like to present you guys with..........<br><br><b> The Opening of the Second Book of Angelfall: A Tragic gif Play! </b> <br><br>Caitlin is walking down the road one day when, sight of all sights, a copy of the Second Angelfall book appears! She was able to maintain her dignity and composure as its tantalizing cover sparkled in the sun <s> yeah, right, she totally freaked out </s>:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681935.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And she just can't resist breaking into song:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681936.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As Caitlin slowly approaches what could be the best book of her life, she places her hands on the cover:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681937.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As her out of control emotions rocket into the stratosphere, she looks around to see if this is a joke:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/461718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seeing that it's not, her fingers slowly inch over to open to the first page; inside, her spirit is elated!:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/470495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While.....on the <i> outside </i> our beautiful, clever, and all-together amazing Caitlin shows a little <i> less </i> restraint......<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681938.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She is finally able to calm herself down enough to re-approach the book; however, after some techniques are used to slow her racing heart:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All of the sudden, the worst happens: the book starts to move away from her! She, of course, chases after it desperately:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/412042.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She can never catch up to it, as much as she runs. Eventually, the book disappears off into the distance, never to be seen again. She is forlorn as tears well in her eyes:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681940.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The road also disintegrates around her, until she wakes up in her desk chair at home, and she realizes that she dreamed the whole thing. The book is still months, maybe even a year, away from being published! It's just too much as she wallows in despair over what could have been:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681941.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She remains forlorn until the book is published, which turns out to be never. If you even ask her about it, this is what happens:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681942.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THE END.<br><br>......<br><br>...........<br><br>.................<br><br>........................<br><br><s> I have an overactive imagination, okay? </s><br><br>And let me just say that if we find out that Penryn is in a relationship with Obi or start developing feelings for him, I'm going to be pissed. Fucking goddamn pissed. And, since this series is supposedly five books long and although that does makes me happy, there is a chance we might not see Raffe at all in the second one and this might just be all about Penryn and the resistance. <s> Just thinking about not seeing Raffe again makes me want to go to a hole somewhere and cry myself into oblivion</s> So it won't happen. Because I said so. Anyways......<br><br>FIN. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051890744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2503669747765955621"><b>4 POOKY BEAR STARS!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410993043i/11180554._SY540_.jpg' alt='Mountain View' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><p>It was quite a good read.But I didn't enjoy this one as much as I did the first book.The beginning was boring and there were some moments that I wanted to put the book down and start another one.The story moved so slowly and it just didn't work out for me.But the other half of the book was quite interesting,not as good as the first book but there were some moments that I quite enjoyed.Also there was a funny moment that I couldn't stop laughing for an hour.That was my favorite </p></span>
  <span id="freeText2503669747765955621" style="display:none"><b>4 POOKY BEAR STARS!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410993043i/11180554._SY540_.jpg" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>It was quite a good read.But I didn't enjoy this one as much as I did the first book.The beginning was boring and there were some moments that I wanted to put the book down and start another one.The story moved so slowly and it just didn't work out for me.But the other half of the book was quite interesting,not as good as the first book but there were some moments that I quite enjoyed.Also there was a funny moment that I couldn't stop laughing for an hour.That was my favorite part of the book.Seriously it was one of the funniest book moments that I had.Beside that there are not a lot of breathtaking moments and the ending is not that unexpected.It was good but not how I wanted it to be.</p><br><br><p>However it was a<b> great book </b>, a powerful story and it blends correctly with the first book.I can't wait for the third book!</p><br><br><i>Okay..Let's talk about the story:<u>(There may be spoilers so if you haven't read the book try to avoid this paragraph)</u></i><br><br><p>This book continues the story of the first one. Penryn now apart from Raffe continues her adventure to protect her family.Her family is not quite normal.Her sister can walk again and there is something off with her that no one knows what.Also she discovers about things that angels are creating and their plans to demolish the earth.</p><br> <br><b>
  <i>Main characters</i>
</b><br><br><b>Penryn</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379799324i/653013._SX540_.jpg" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>What I liked about Penryn in this book is her courage to do things on her own.Also her modesty because she never accepted that she is some kind of a hero.Also the motivation she carries with herself is remarkable because even when her world is all falling apart she is determined to protect the people she loves.</p><br><br><b>Raffe</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410993043i/11180555._SX540_.jpg" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>Well as I mention in the review of the first book I really like Raffe's sence of humor.There are some sentences that you can't continue without bursting into laughter.</p><br><br><b>Paige</b><br><br><p>Paige is one of my favorite characters in this book.Her new transformation makes her like a killing machine and I really like killing machines.</p><br><br><b>
  <i>Me while reading the book ( favorite sentences ) :</i>
</b><br><br><blockquote>“I look up to say something but he puts his finger to my lips and whispers, “Don’t talk. You’ll just spoil my fantasy of rescuing an innocent damsel in distress as soon as you open your mouth.” </blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425768ra/850021.gif" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>“He glares at me as if he already hates it. “What is it?” I consider lying but what’s the point? I didn’t know.” <br>“I’ve mentioned that names have power, right? Do you realize that when she fights battles, she’s going to have to announce herself to the opposing sword? Because you've never seen me afraid” </blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401496641ra/9811151.gif" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>“You're naming your collector's-item, kick-ass sword that's made to maim and kill, specifically designed to bring your ginormous enemies to their knees and hear the lamentation of their women-Pooky Bear?"<br>"Yeah, you like it?” </blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410993043ra/11180558.gif" alt="Mountain View" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>“You broke me out of the grasp of a living horror when I thought all hope was gone.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_571233307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571233307" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571233307?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=angels-demons">angels-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=saved-the-genre">saved-the-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=badass-mc">badass-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=mc-you-can-root-for">mc-you-can-root-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571233307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16551061781689764269"><b>*SPOILER-FREE*</b><br/><br/>Picture this: the world ends, and you’re left with a schizophrenic mother who’s fallen off the deep end and a kid sister that looks like an autopsy victim with razor-blade teeth. <br/><br/>The humans around you are half-convinced that you’re hellspawn due to an unfortunate rising-from-the-dead incident, your one non-familial ally now looks like a creature from your nightmares, and since he also thinks that you’re <i>actually</i> dead, he’s abandoned you. <br/><br/>Now you’re being carted off to God-knows-whe</span>
  <span id="freeText16551061781689764269" style="display:none"><b>*SPOILER-FREE*</b><br /><br />Picture this: the world ends, and you’re left with a schizophrenic mother who’s fallen off the deep end and a kid sister that looks like an autopsy victim with razor-blade teeth. <br /><br />The humans around you are half-convinced that you’re hellspawn due to an unfortunate rising-from-the-dead incident, your one non-familial ally now looks like a creature from your nightmares, and since he also thinks that you’re <i>actually</i> dead, he’s abandoned you. <br /><br />Now you’re being carted off to God-knows-where with a group of wounded, dirty survivors that are probably half a step away from turning cannibal. Things can’t get much worse, can they? <br /><br /><b>WRONG.</b><br /><br />Things can always get worse. I just didn’t realize how <i>much</i> worse they’d get in a YA novel. I have to say, I love that Ee took it to the place she did. There’s a darkness in this book that clings to the pages, slithers from the paper to seep up your fingers and wrap its icy tendrils around your heart as you read. <br /><br />This book is terrifying, but not in the way you might expect. Sure, there are some suspenseful moments, and more than a few scenes that will get your adrenaline going, but the real horror in this story comes from a surprising source. Not the angelic invaders, not the monsters that come buzzing out of the darkness in this latest installment, but the humans. <br /><br />We think we’re so advanced, with our smart phones and our global connections. So above the rest of the animals on this planet. But take away our modernity, starve us for a little while and lock us in a cage, and you begin to realize why we’ve climbed to the top. It’s because we’re ruthless. Savage. At our core, we’re still fueled by the primitive need to survive, and this book serves as a haunting reminder of the things we’re capable of and the depths we’ll descend to. <br /><br />Penryn is a survivor in the true sense of the word. She’s what so many other heroines in this genre claim to be and fail to achieve. She’s ruthless. Savage. And absolutely <i>believable</i>. She’ll do anything for herself and her family. <br /><br />This makes her a complicated character by nature and one not everyone might warm to because those same instincts drive her to put herself and those she loves above all others. She has to make hard decisions in this book, has to choose which battles to fight, and those choices were part of what made this such a compelling read.<br /><br />So prepare yourself, because this book pulls no punches. It picks up the blink after its predecessor ended and provides the same non-stop action, the same gritty, dirty and sometimes ugly story of post-apocalyptic survival. This is easily my favorite YA series of all time and after this latest installment I have infinite faith in Susan Ee to continue to deliver.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16551061781689764269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11046754294739563827" style="display:none">I was rather disappointed with this sequel because I didn’t find it as exciting an action packed as Angelfall. This may have something to do with Raffe and Penryn not being very exciting apart from each other, because for the first half of the book, I struggled to stay interested. On the positive side, the second half does pick up after Penryn and Raffe reunites and the horror aspect that we saw at the end of Angelfall really starts to shine through. I’m curious to see where this series is going, because a large part of World After was about Penryn — once again — going off into danger to save her sister, who seems to now have a larger role in this whole Angel Apocalypse thing. I really hope books 3-6 don’t follow similar plots.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_628233818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/628233818" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/628233818?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=to-read-upcoming-releases">to-read-upcoming-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=apocalypse">apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer628233818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2740951396772874712">*no spoilers*<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Was that you, Pooky Bear?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>There are a lot of themes of good vs. bad, the nature of evil, the length of which man will go to survive. As far as I'm concerned, the only message in this book that mattered is: <b>you do NOT fuck with my sister, because I will hunt you down and I will make you pay</b>. I understand it, and I admire Penryn for it.<br/><br/>I have a baby sister, I love her. We are the same age apart as Penryn and Paige.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385015967i/7045776.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>...aaaand some years after.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385015967i/7045777.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It hasn't always been smooth sail</span>
  <span id="freeText2740951396772874712" style="display:none">*no spoilers*<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Was that you, Pooky Bear?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>There are a lot of themes of good vs. bad, the nature of evil, the length of which man will go to survive. As far as I'm concerned, the only message in this book that mattered is: <b>you do NOT fuck with my sister, because I will hunt you down and I will make you pay</b>. I understand it, and I admire Penryn for it.<br><br>I have a baby sister, I love her. We are the same age apart as Penryn and Paige.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385015967i/7045776.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...aaaand some years after.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385015967i/7045777.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It hasn't always been smooth sailing, but I will do everything I can to make damn sure she has a happy life. Nobody hurts my baby sister. A good sibling vengeance story will get me every time. I loved it in the <i>Fever</i> series, and I love it in this book.<br><br>I really enjoyed this book...with some reservations. This is one of the situations where I find myself to be the odd man out. I think every single one of my friend loved the first book in this series, whereas I enjoyed the originality of the first book, but was largely indifferent to it. However, I'm happy to find that I liked this book a lot more than the first. Don't get me wrong, there was absolutely nothing I disliked about this book. Penryn is a strong female character, with a tremendous sense of morality and loyalty to her family and friends that I admire, and the romance was well done in that it developed over time and was not the focus of the book. I had some problems with the plot, particularly towards the second half of the book, but overall, I think my reaction to the book is just one of chemistry.<br><br>That's right, chemistry. It happens with people, and apparently, it happens with books and the characters within. In life, you meet a lot of people. Some, you like, for no fucking reason. Some, you hate on the spot, despite the fact that they are perfectly pleasant, perfectly nice, completely inoffensive whatsoever, and yet, try as you might...there's just something lacking that prevents you from completely liking, from completely enjoying that person's company.<br><br>For me, the <i>Angelfall</i> series is a perfect example of chemistry gone wrong. <b>This book has pretty much everything I could ever want, action, a light romance, awesome characters, horror, death, blood. SO MUCH BLOOD.</b> And yet...like, not love. What can I say? It's just chemistry.<br><br>I'm starting to sound like I don't like this book. That's not true! I liked it a lot. I just find myself largely indifferent to the characters; that is a matter <b>purely of personal taste, and not a reflection on the book itself</b>. I truly did enjoy this book.<br><br><u>Summary</u>: I didn't remember much from the first book. I didn't need to. This book summarizes the ending of the previous book well enough so that I didn't have any trouble being reimmersed into the World After. We are back in the Silicon Valley and it it a fucking (glorious) mess. This is what I loved. This is what I wanted. This is what I didn't get much of from the first book. People are scared, hungry, in hiding. They're forming into groups, gangs, because you can't survive alone, not in a world like this. Penryn, broken Paige, and their schizophrenic mother have just escaped the aerie, and are with the Resistance, planning to slowly retake their world from the destructive Angels. Penryn has no idea where Raffe is. All she gets is flashes of his thoughts and dreams, projected by the sword he has left her. <b>Raffe is so tantalizingly close, yet so far away.</b><br><br>It's a tough life made tougher when Paide, Penryn's broken sister gets kidnapped. Penryn will do anything to get her back.<br><br><u>The Plot &amp; Setting</u>: A lot better this time around. Things just made more sense, and there is more of what I wanted to see. Call me morbid, but I love reading about a broken world. It's what drew me into post-apocalyptic fiction, and dystopian fiction. It's what hooked me in <i>The Walking Dead</i>, and I felt that this book delivered that scenario so much more than the previous one. We get to see more of the remnants of society as they cower in fear and try to raise a meager resistance. We get to see people imprisoned, starving, willing to go to the extent of cannibalism because they are so desperate for sustence. It is a gripping setting and scenario, it's not overly detailed on a grander scale, since Penryn only knows what she sees, so it is fine with me.<br><br>This book moves fast. There is too much action at times, for me, because I'm the sort of person who needs a moment of quiet and introspection amidst all the chaos. I still HATE the concept of the Aerie. The thought of angels getting into frat boy parties and swigging champagne and chilling with gorgeous "daughters of men," was absurd to me in the previous book, and it remains completely stupid to me in this book.<br><br><b>I liked the fact that this book did not feel the need to force Penryn and Raffe together unnecessarily</b>. It shows that Penryn is independent, it shows that she is capable of survival without Raffe, however foolhardy her actions are, at times. And it makes the eventual reappeance of Raffe so much better, when it finally happens. It felt like taking a deep breath after holding it in for so long.<br><blockquote>
  <i>I look up to say something but he puts his finger to my lips and whispers, “Don’t talk. You’ll just spoil my fantasy of rescuing an innocent damsel in distress as soon as you open your mouth.”</i>
</blockquote>^____________^<br><br><u>The Characters</u>: I liked most of them. I really enjoyed Penryn's character, she is strong, she means well, but she is imperfect, and so very human. Penryn makes foolish decisions, she makes mistakes, and she realizes those mistakes. I liked that about her. <b>Penryn knows all too well that no matter how good your intentions, no matter how bravely you try to act, no matter how much of a hero you try to me, shit can always go wrong.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I feel sick.<br>Sick from fear. Sick from anger. Sick from the stupidity of what I’ve done.<br>I came here for my sister and instead I’ve gotten myself recklessly caught.</i>
</blockquote>I liked the other characters in the book, and how well they were portrayed. They don't appear for too long, but the twins, Dum and Dee greatly reminded me of <i>Poison Study</i>'s Ari and and Janco, the "Power Twins." <b>Dum and Dee are strong, tough guys, who often act exaggeratedly silly, and they inject just the right amount of humor into a serious book.</b><br><br>I find myself altogether fascinated and horrified by Paige and Penryn's intrepid, unstoppable, and completely insane mother. She is truly bulletproof, and I can only shake my head, aghast, at her actions throughout the story.<br><br><u>The Romance</u>: Penryn is not altogether strong, she has her moments of weakness. She aches, thinking about Raffe but there are better things to think about. Priorities, Penryn has them! <b>Penryn allows herself a few moments of wanting him and missing him, but really, it's the end of the world, and she ain't got no time for romance when her SISTER's missing.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>I’m dying to know what he felt during our kiss.<br>I know it doesn’t matter. I know it won’t change anything. I know it’s juvenile.<br>Whatever.<br>Can’t a girl be a girl for, like, five minutes?</i>
</blockquote>I felt the romance was very well done; it was light, it was believable, and I love the fact that Ms. Ee has the courage to not force Penryn and Raffe together unbelievably and unnecessarily.<br><br>Altogether, a really good book, with likeable characters, in an interesting setting. <b>You want your kick-ass heroine, you got your kick-ass heroine.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2740951396772874712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_249466643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249466643" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249466643?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249466643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12396727544620393976"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12983100.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_' title='World After (Penryn & the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>World After</a> ticks a lot of boxes but it simply isn't as strong a story as we were given in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a>. I don't know how many books are planned for this series but it seems to fall prey to what would be called "middle book syndrome" in a trilogy. The story plods along, giving the novel a weighted feel which made it easy to put aside at times (something that could never be said for the previous book). My rating leans towards the positive because I did enjoy this sequel - Ee has a talen</span>
  <span id="freeText12396727544620393976" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12983100.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_" title="World After (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a> ticks a lot of boxes but it simply isn't as strong a story as we were given in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>. I don't know how many books are planned for this series but it seems to fall prey to what would be called "middle book syndrome" in a trilogy. The story plods along, giving the novel a weighted feel which made it easy to put aside at times (something that could never be said for the previous book). My rating leans towards the positive because I did enjoy this sequel - Ee has a talent for balancing gory, gritty action scenes with playful and hilarious banter - but I admit that I was expecting something more from possibly my most anticipated book of this year. Still, the last fifty pages exploded with flashes of everything I love - action, humour, unexpected plot turns and romance - and I adore Penryn enough to know I will be returning for more.<br><br>Readers will surely recognise the author's delightfully sarcastic touches of humour straight away - I found myself laughing aloud multiple times, even when I'd been cringing in horror and sat tense on the edge of my seat just moments earlier. I think this is what I like most about Ee's writing: she somehow manages to make it both creepy and funny at the same time. This rarely works for me; I almost always find the humour draining the scary atmosphere out of each scene or the jokes falling flat amid the descriptions of gore... but Ee makes it work perfectly. Penryn is as badass as ever, always in the centre of the battle and fighting for the ones she loves. Raffe also returns (though not often enough if you ask me) for hilarity and sexual tension.<br><br>My main issue is the lack of progression in this book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> took us on a wild journey that presented us with so much fascinating information, angel lore and complexly-woven characters and relationships. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12983100.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_" title="World After (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a>, on the other hand, takes baby steps and reminds us of many things we already know: that Penryn feels conflicted about her newly monstrous sister, that she and Raffe have the hots for one another, etc, etc. While it wasn't a bad read, I felt like it could have all happened in a few chapters rather than spread over an entire book. The greatest progress made by this sequel is in the character development of Penryn's mother. She becomes more than the token crazy person in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12983100.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_" title="World After (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a> and we see her for what she really is: a confused but intelligent woman who loves her children very dearly. This aspect of the book was fantastic, IMO.<br><br>A good sequel that could have been better with more careful plotting and pacing - perhaps the author intends this series to be longer than it needs to be (as is often the case). But I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12983100.World_After__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___2_" title="World After (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #2) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">World After</a> a lot and I'm not surprised to see other reviewers expressing their continued love. I just hope the third book doesn't take so long!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12396727544620393976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751559.gif' alt=' photo excited_zpsbe25007c.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>As I was reading:<br/><a href='http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/carltondancing_zpsd6401aea.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751560.gif' alt=' photo carltondancing_zpsd6401aea.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When</span>
  <span id="freeText16657214686260463685" style="display:none"><b>Scroll down for my full review.</b><br><br>My initial thoughts on 9/18/13:<br><br>On Friday, when I got my ARC of <i>World After</i>:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/Entangled_zps9ee97b56.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751554.gif" alt=" photo Entangled_zps9ee97b56.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Also, because Amazon actually sent me an ARC!!!:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/holy-sht_zps5d58f8ff.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751555.gif" alt=" photo holy-sht_zps5d58f8ff.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Friday night when I got home and sat down to crack this baby open:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/mybodyisready_zpsec4f6e8b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751556.gif" alt=" photo mybodyisready_zpsec4f6e8b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When my family wanted to go out to dinner, then shopping, then a million other things that weren't reading:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/crazyeye_zps18662eca.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751557.gif" alt=" photo crazyeye_zps18662eca.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>All weekend, when my family had other plans for my precious reading time:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/nerdrage_zpsdcc6139d.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751558.gif" alt=" photo nerdrage_zpsdcc6139d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then on Sunday when I finally got to start reading:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/excited_zpsbe25007c.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751559.gif" alt=" photo excited_zpsbe25007c.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As I was reading:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/carltondancing_zpsd6401aea.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751560.gif" alt=" photo carltondancing_zpsd6401aea.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When Raffe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[finally <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> made his first appearance:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/hithere_zps771df093.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751561.gif" alt=" photo hithere_zps771df093.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Last night when I finished the book:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/nowords_zps2342737a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751562.gif" alt=" photo nowords_zps2342737a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And then when I realized I have to wait FOREVER for the next book:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/sulking_zpsb38b022e.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751563.gif" alt=" photo sulking_zpsb38b022e.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Overall impression:<br><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/gifs/thumpingheart_zps28793cba.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380390061ra/751564.gif" alt=" photo thumpingheart_zps28793cba.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>__________________________________________<br><br><br><blockquote>"Everyone thinks I'm dead."</blockquote><br>And so begins the sequel to one of the best angel books I've ever read.  I knew <i>World After</i> would be good.  I mean, how could the follow-up to <i>
  <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/01/audiobook-review-angelfall-by-susan-ee.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>
</i> be anything <i>but </i>good? This sequel has been a long time coming, though some have been waiting longer than others.  (I only discovered <i>Angelfall </i>last year, but it quickly became a favorite.)  To put all of your dear minds at rest, I'll just say that this book was <b>well</b> worth the wait.<br><br><b>
  <u>Penryn</u>
</b><br><blockquote>"My dad once told me life would get complicated when I grew up.  I'm guessing this isn't what he meant.  My mom, on the other hand, agreed with him, and I'm guessing this kind of thing is exactly what she meant."</blockquote><br>I am ridiculously happy that after everything Penryn Young has suffered, she came through it all with her snark intact.  I probably flagged a hundred passages in my ARC, including those highlighting her quick wit, her sharp-tounged quips, and her banter with Raffe.  But I also loved her inner monologues, where she pondered how best to escape an inescapable situation, how to protect her family, and what to make of her feelings for Raffe.<br><br>I voted Penryn to the top of my "favorite heroines ever" list the very first time I read <i>Angelfall</i>, but I've come to appreciate her character even more with this sequel.  Not only is she a skilled fighter who would do anything and risk anything to keep her family safe, but she's also very smart and calculating, and she has a remarkable talent for keeping cool in situations that would find anyone else running for the hills with their tail between their legs.  Penryn is the epitome of what I want in a protagonist because even though she is all these things, she is still just a girl, emotional and vulnerable and just trying to make it to the next day.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Sword</u>
</b><br><blockquote>"I've mentioned that names have power, right?  Do you realize that when she fights battles, she's going to have to announce herself to the opposing sword?  She'll be forced to say something ridiculous like, 'I am Pooky Bear, from an ancient line of archangel swords.'  Or, 'Bow down to me, Pooky Bear, who has only two other equals in all the worlds.'"  He shakes his head.  "How is she going to get any respect?"</blockquote><br>Yes, the Sword of Light gets its own section in my review because it is <i>that</i> badass.  This thing is sentient, can tell who's got a hold of it and what their intentions are, and it. Is. Badass.  Okay, I said that already, but I just need to convey <i>how</i> awesome this sword is.  And Penryn has to hide her.<br><br>The disguise Penryn comes up with is, well, degrading and demoralizing to the sword and anyone who knows exactly what it is.  As is the name Penryn accidentally gives it.  Those were some of my favorite parts in the story because not only did they show how connected to the sword Penryn already was, they also added some much-needed levity to an otherwise disheartening story.<br><br><b>
  <u>Raffe</u>
</b><br><blockquote>"Something catches his eye and he walks to the window.  A formation of angels flies past the moon.  He leans toward the glass, almost pressing his face to it as he looks up at the angels. Every line of him tells me he longs to fly with them."</blockquote><br>Raffe is, for better or worse, absent from a good chunk of the book.  BUT, through the sentient power of that awesome, badass sword, we get glimpses of him in the past, sort of like his perspective through the sword's eyes.  So, even though he's not <i>there</i>, he's still with us.  I think it's because of this -- and her fear for her family -- that Penryn is able to continue, to keep going when it all seems pointless.<br><blockquote>"Raffe looks over at the bloody knife in my hand.  "If I still had any doubts that it was you, that would do it."  He gestures toward my opponent rolling on the ground with his hands cradling his package."</blockquote><br>When Raffe does resurface, he is every bit the Raffe we met before.  He still wants his wings back, and now he's fighting with a rage that only comes from grief.  He believed Penryn to be dead, and so he undertook his previous mission with single-minded intensity.  Raffe can be hard and cruel and unforgiving, but he is not wholly unfeeling.  In fact, I believe there's more emotion locked up in his angel heart than we're ready to see yet, which is why we've only been given glimpses so far.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Romance</u>
</b><br><blockquote>"The candlelight flickers a soft glow along his jawline, along his lips.  "I hated losing her."  His voice is a low growl.  "I hadn't realized just how attached I'd gotten."  He reaches and moves a strand of wet hair out of my face.  "How dangerously addictive she could be."</blockquote><br>Le sigh.  I'll tell you what's addictive:  everything about Raffe.  Between his quips about Penryn being a lowly human to the condescending way he berates her every action, you'd think he can't stand her.  But quite to the contrary, this is a defense mechanism.  Push her away so that he's not tempted to make the same mistakes his Watchers did.  I get it.  And it's kind of hot to watch the tension between these two, even knowing it won't amount to anything...yet.  That's the thing...all those long looks and all of that banter, they're leading up to something big.  I can feel it.  Raffe can feel it.  Even Penryn, who thinks Raffe has no feelings for her, feels it...she just doesn't quite grasp what it means yet.  The sword helps her along that path, though.  ;0)<br><br><b>
  <u>Penryn's Family</u>
</b><br><blockquote>"He sighs.  "I miss the days when females could be ordered around and they'd have no choice."<br>"Sure that wasn't just a myth?  I'm pretty sure nobody ever ordered my mom around -- ever."<br>"You're probably right.  The unruliness of the women in your family must go back for generations.  You're like a plague upon the land."</blockquote><br>For those of you wondering, yes, Penryn's mother is <s>just as crazy,</s> dare I say EVEN crazier than she was in the first book.  That woman gives <i>new meaning</i> to the word crazy.  And yet, this series just would not be the same without her.  Far from being a detriment to all of Penryn's well-laid plans, she actually makes things easier for Penryn...more often than not, anyway.  Her antics tend to keep everyone occupied while Penryn does all the heavy lifting.<br><br>Paige is more feared than even their mother now, though, and so Penryn spends a good chunk of time battling her feelings toward her sister and also clashing with others, all in an effort to keep little Paige safe. But the changes inflicted on Paige in the first book have left her stronger and more capable, and it's time Penryn gave her the benefit of the doubt.<br><br>Everything else in this novel is just icing on the cake.  Beliel, Obi, and Dee Dum are all present and accounted for, and causing the kind of trouble you'd expect from all of them.  Penryn gets herself into a jam a time or two...or ten.  Plans are being cemented for the evil angels to fully possess our world and everything it has to offer.  And all the while I'm screaming at Raffe to give us some hope.<br><br>If you enjoyed <i>Angelfall</i>, I have no doubt you'll love this sequel equally as much.  The writing, the characters, the world...everything you fell in love with in the first book is present and accounted for, only it plucks an even more emotional response from the reader this time around because you already know and love these characters.  You've seen what they've survived, what they're willing to do for each other, and you just want them to be okay in the end.  And you also know that it's going to be a long, long wait for the next book.<br><br>Bring on the <i>Angelfall </i>movie already!!!<br><br>*<i>All quotes were taken from an ARC and are subject to change.</i><br><br><i>Super huge thanks to Skyscape/Amazon Children's Publishing for providing an ARC for review!</i>.<br><br>This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/11/review-world-after-by-susan-ee.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_383119808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383119808" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383119808?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383119808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11082135552201919587"><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><b>WARNING:</b> There will probably be spoilers for the first book (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a>) in this review. <br/><br/>I read the first book of this series about three years ago. I had my doubts about it, since it looked like some typical dystopian/paranormal romance, but a lot of reviewers were saying it had far exceeded their expectations, so I gave it a try.<br/><br/>And I was pleasantly surprised! <i>Angelfall</i> turned out to be a dark and atmosphe</span>
  <span id="freeText11082135552201919587" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>WARNING:</b> There will probably be spoilers for the first book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>) in this review. <br><br>I read the first book of this series about three years ago. I had my doubts about it, since it looked like some typical dystopian/paranormal romance, but a lot of reviewers were saying it had far exceeded their expectations, so I gave it a try.<br><br>And I was pleasantly surprised! <i>Angelfall</i> turned out to be a dark and atmospheric book, full of intriguing world-building, disturbing and vivid imagery, a lot of action and excitement, a likable and fairly well-developed romance, and a cool heroine. <br><br>I waited eagerly for the sequel to come out, especially since the first book ended on a bit of a cliffhanger. I pre-ordered the e-book and attacked it the moment it magically appeared on my Kindle.<br><br>And, well ... I liked it. Don't get me wrong, it's a good book. It just didn't pack the same punch as the first book, in my opinion. In the end, I had very mixed feelings about it. It's now been more than a year since I read it (I'm sorry, this review is EXTREMELY delayed due to me being busy with college and also being a lazy shit), so my memory is a little cloudy. But from what I remember, here are my thoughts.<br><br><b>
  <u>What I liked:</u>
</b><br><br>• <b>Action! Excitement!</b> –– If anything, this book is a page-turner. Like the first book, it has a lot of violence and action. There were definitely a lot of sequences that had me on the edge of my seat.<br>• <b>Family dynamics</b> –– Penryn's mother and her sister, Paige, were mostly absent throughout <i>Angelfall</i>, so I liked that they played more of a role in the sequel. We get to experience more of their relationships with each other (which is all very complicated, what with the mother suffering from some kind of mental illness and Paige being a ... cannibalistic demon thing ... ?) <br>• <b>The humor</b> –– Something I appreciated about the first book was the dark humor, which is still present in this one. (For example, Penryn carries around a sword hidden in a giant teddy bear named Pooky Bear––maybe a little a bit ridiculous and unreasonable, but the idea is still amusing.) <br>• <b>The romance doesn't overwhelm the story</b> –– Well, I have mixed feelings about this. I think there could have been a <i>bit</i> more romance, but I'm also glad it didn't take over the story. It could've gone down the route that a lot of YA series take––where the protagonist gets together with the love interest and then it's just a ton of making out and drama and love triangles and whatnot. Fortunately that's not the case here. There's still that hint of romance, but without distracting too much from the actual conflict.<br><br><b>
  <u>What didn't work for me:</u>
</b><br><br>• <b>The pacing</b> –– This book is 320 pages which is not <i>that</i> short, but when I remember it I feel like it was much shorter. I think it's just that it took a while to really get into the heart of the story. As I said, it had exciting parts, but it didn't feel as fast-paced as the first book was. It just felt like a lot of build-up rather than having its own strong, central plot. The end seemed to be moving towards a more significant conflict, but then it was cut off abruptly.<br>• <b>WHERE THE HELL WAS RAFFE?</b> –– Raffe was one of my favorite parts of the first book, so I was pretty disappointed that he didn't show up until more than halfway through this one. And when he did show up, the reunion between him and Penryn was ... anti-climatic. I mean, he thought she was dead and then when they met up again it was just kind of like:<br><br><b>Penryn:</b> hi I'm not dead<br><b>Raffe:</b> coolbeans<br><br>Like seriously, that's it???? The scene where he thought she was dying/dead in the first book was so heart-wrenching, and then the whole thing where he returned her (supposedly dead) body to her mother even though it could've gotten him killed ... it was just AGGGH MY HEART. ALL THE FEELINGS.<br><br>So ... I expected something a little more emotional, I guess. <br><br>Additionally, I feel like one of the strongest things about <i>Angelfall</i> was the dynamic between Raffe and Penryn––their "witty banter," the development of their relationship, etc. And since they were separated for most of the sequel, that aspect was mostly absent. But now that they've been reunited, maybe the third book will be better.<br><br><b>
  <u>The final word:</u>
</b><br><br>I had super high expectations for this book, and I have to say they weren't quite met. But that said, it was still enjoyable and exciting, and I still have hope for the third one. <br><br><br>---------<br><br><b>Pre-review rambling and whatnot under the cut:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>After reading:</b><br><br>Acccck. I'm like ... really torn. Because I did enjoy this a lot, but ... I don't know, I guess I was expecting a lot from it because I waited like two whole years. And it is really good, but I felt like just when it was getting to the good stuff it just kind of stopped out of nowhere and that frustrated me. But yeah, don't get me wrong; I did really like it. Review coming soon-ish. <br><br>--------<br>--------<br><br><b>Before reading:</b><br><br>Update (11/11/13):<br><br>*Deep breath* A week from tomorrow. A WEEK FROM TOMORROW. WE CAN DO IT, GUYS. JUST HANG IN THERE. AAHHHHH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383164879ra/6422755.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Update (8/26/13):<br><br>AAAHHH THE COVER AT LAST. IT'S SO BEAUTIFULLLL. *FANGIRLS ALL OVER THE PLACE* <br><br>You can get a closer look at it and read an excerpt <a href="http://shelf-life.ew.com/2013/08/26/susan-ee-world-after-cover-angelfall-exclusive/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!<br><br>Update (6/22/13):<br><br>The release date was changed to November 19th. UGGHHHHH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681954.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, at least there's a real release date now.<br><br>... But I'm still waiting on that cover.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380250663ra/681955.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>---------------<br>---------------<br><br>Update (5/30/13):<br><br>Haha okay, apparently the release date was a lie and there's no official one yet. POOOP.<br><br>BUT, BUT THERE'S A TITLE. AND THERE'S A DESCRIPTION. OH MY GOD, FINALLY!!!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/569353.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>---------------<br>---------------<br><br>Update (4/14/13):<br><br>OCTOBER 10TH.<br><br>Well, that's still rather far away. *Sigh* But at least we have an official release date.<br><br>NOW HOW ABOUT THAT TITLE AND A COVER AND DESCRIPTION AND ALL THAT JAZZ. :)<br><br>---------------<br>---------------<br><br>Patiently waiting for this book to come out.<br><br><b>In 2013.</b><br><br>I'll just be right here...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/372381.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461103747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17617343460916352499"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“You broke me out of the grasp of a living horror when I thought all hope was gone. You gave me the opportunity to crawl back to life when no one else could. You're a hero, Penryn, whether you like it or not.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Blurb: Penryn drives through the streets of San Francisco looking for Paige. Why are the streets so empty? Where is everybody? Her search leads her into the heart of the angels' secret plans where she catches a glimpse of their motivations, and learns the horrifying extent to which the </span>
  <span id="freeText17617343460916352499" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“You broke me out of the grasp of a living horror when I thought all hope was gone. You gave me the opportunity to crawl back to life when no one else could. You're a hero, Penryn, whether you like it or not.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Blurb: Penryn drives through the streets of San Francisco looking for Paige. Why are the streets so empty? Where is everybody? Her search leads her into the heart of the angels' secret plans where she catches a glimpse of their motivations, and learns the horrifying extent to which the angels are willing to go.<br>Meanwhile, Raffe hunts for his wings. Without them, he can't rejoin the angels, can't take his rightful place as one of their leaders. When faced with recapturing his wings or helping Penryn survive, which will he choose?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444681798ra/16534872.gif" width="500" height="234" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>World After takes places straight after the events in Angelfall and we get to see not only Penryn’s story but also a little bit of Raffe’s and also what happened to Paige.<br><br>I don’t know if this book was better than Angelfall or not but that’s because we see less of Raffe and I missed his interaction with Penryn; also, this book is slower than the first one and I got a bit bored in some parts, I’m not going to lie but I really liked this book. <br><br>The characters were as captivating as in Angelfall and the writing style continued being simplistic, and while this book doesn’t add much plot to the story, I enjoyed reading.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427565893ra/14285759.gif" width="500" height="239" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were a lot of things that worked flawlessly in WA, such as the humor, the character development and the setting but Penryn rocked the fuck out of this book one more time.<br><br>I was surprised to find a kinda different Penryn. Her feelings toward her sister, her world, Raffe and herself evolved in a really pleasant and logic way. She acknowledges she misses Raffe, she acknowledges her sister will never be normal again and she knows she has to do something. Penryn has definitely grown in very subtle yet strong ways and she just keeps getting better and better.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>She never once stopped being smart but she’s somewhat kinder she just leveled up nicely and it was such a joy reading her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404327753ra/10225875.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Remember how I wanted to have a Raffe’s POV? Well, I didn’t exactly get that but, since we weren’t going to have much of him, I understood the whys of the dreams. And it worked. I feel that this time there was a solid connection with Raffe that helped us looking at him a little bit differently when he showed up. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434910658ra/15277404.gif" width="500" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now I have a soft spot for him and that didn’t happen in the last book so things are good between us right now but I still need a full Raffe’s POV! Come on! Gimme something to work with. I need to love him even when Penryn isn’t on the picture.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You're not Fallen are you?"<br>"From everything I've heard, that would just make me more sexy to you Daughters of Men. What is it that you all see in bad boys?”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Penryn and Raffe as a couple work for me. I think they are really great for each other and Jesus, they could be really sexy but I don’t know if I should ship them because Penryn is only seventeen and Raffe is fucking Archangel Raphael and he’s older than life. Leaving the gods aside, I think this is the biggest age gap I’ve seen and while they’re absolutely amazing, I don’t know how to feel. <u>Someone tell me what to feel.</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435255388ra/15322554.gif" width="500" height="278" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked learning what Paige had to endure, <i>sort of</i>, and what was done to her. And when it comes to Penryn’s mother, well, she’s crazy as fuck but she gets things done. She may be crazy but she isn’t stupid at all and a lot of things she does make sense.<br><br>And come on, you gotta respect a woman who makes grown ass men being scared of her like most people were.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i> “We Young girls are getting a reputation.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>We still don’t know exactly why the apocalypse is so important to the angels. I mean, yes, they want Judgement Day so some of the Fallen may return but why would the angels create all these creatures? It’s obvious they want to eradicate all the humans but <b>do they want Earth for them?</b> And why? I mean, they got Heaven and Hell and they’re so fucking pompous they’d want slaves and all of that so they need humans for that. And what about God? <b>Is God aware of what angels are doing?</b> <br><br>It’s all a bloody mess and now Paige is like the Scorpion Queen and Ultimate Destroyer or something like that and she and Penryn and Raffe are going where…?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437264918ra/15561299.gif" width="472" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gods, and that sword? I didn’t know if I was going to be a fan of it showing dreams to Penryn and all of that but I really liked it at the end. I think it was cool and it was a really useful tool, not only for Penryn but for the plotline as well.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“What, the other swords quake in their scabbards when they see her?”<br> “Yes, if you must know. She was made for ultimate respect. How is she supposed to get that disguised as a teddy bear in a bridal gown?”<br>“It’s not a bridal gown, it’s a skirt for her scabbard. And it’s cute.”<br>“She hates cute. She wants to maim and scar cute.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I missed Penryn and Raffe together *sighs*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421792732ra/13416353.gif" width="499" height="232" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall I enjoyed World After but I didn’t love it as much as Angelfall. I’m still very excited about the last book and how things end up for the characters and the world.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17617343460916352499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
