  <span id="freeText6435318142098010924" style="display:none"><b>So excited to read this <u>AGAIN</u> in April 27 2015.<br /><br />Buddy Reading with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5028851-cathryn" rel="nofollow noopener">Cathryn</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27695727-danae" rel="nofollow noopener">Danae</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29787548-ashley-the-hufflepuff-kitten" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashley</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4255477-angela" rel="nofollow noopener">Angela</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31718503-tanya" rel="nofollow noopener">Tanya</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3344685-sarah" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18104163-navessa" rel="nofollow noopener">Navessa</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8169059-brigid-is-a-massive-coffee-addict" rel="nofollow noopener">Brigid</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131373021" rel="nofollow noopener">Shandra</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10980280-ya" rel="nofollow noopener">Ya</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh" rel="nofollow noopener">Andrea</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/21715922-mindy" rel="nofollow noopener">Mindy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30527687-maria" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12045894-annette-booknerderie" rel="nofollow noopener">Annette</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8409451-kristen" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31239385-lea" rel="nofollow noopener">Lea</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10992510-sara" rel="nofollow noopener">Sara</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer" rel="nofollow noopener">Athena (Shardbearer)</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3250652-brandi" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandi</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7214073-nicholas" rel="nofollow noopener">Nicholas</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9026138-michelle-book-hangovers" rel="nofollow noopener">Michelle</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11494588-tandie" rel="nofollow noopener">Tandie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1913825-jenny" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5220112-amanda" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin" rel="nofollow noopener">Gavin</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina" rel="nofollow noopener">Armina</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/25393430-sh3lly-not-all-those-who-wander-are-lost" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelly</a> at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br /></b><br /><br />Reread April 27:<br /><br />Darker than I remember and I loved it. Susan Ee really builds in some horrific elements about how bad it can really get. I'm all refreshed now and ready for the conclusion.<br /><br /><b>Original review Nov 2013</b><br /><br />4.5 Stars Wow just wow. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The world going crazy doesn’t mean your mother isn’t still crazy too.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I thought Angelfall was a wild ride but World After kicked crazy up a notch. Susan Ee has really impressed me with her second book in the Penryn and The End of Days series. After the first book I really wanted some insight into the Angels and Raffe’s Past, I also wanted to know more about the creepy Frankenstein monsters that were at the Aerie, Penryn’s crazy mom and Paige poor little Paige. Well Susan Ee found a great way to give us insight into most of these things and just when I thought she couldn’t horrify me any more Ms. Ee pushed the bar just one step farther. <br /><br />Penryn’s mom is still crazy, I mean sometimes she seems like maybe she is the only one that is on top of what is truly happening but she is still nuts and I love every second of it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>”Of course your fine.” She keeps walking. “You’re the devils bride and these are his creatures.”</i>
</b> - <i>Penryn’s Mom</i><br /><br />In Penryn’s mom’s defense the tableau at the end of Angelfall did make Raffe look like the Devil. But, you still have to be crazy to come up with an idea like that. It is safe to say that the Young family wasn’t exactly popular in the new resistance camp with a mom speaking in tongues, resurrected girl and a stitched up child with super strength and razor teeth. <br /><br />DeeDum were hilarious and up to their shenanigans again at the new resistance camp. They have some great one liners and seems to always be in the know, but that is to be expected of the great spymasters. Where ever they go trouble will abound but they seem to always be able to help Penryn out in some way.<br /><br />Even though Raffe and Penryn are apart at the beginning of the book Susan Ee found a very interesting way to show us part of Raffe’s past as an Archangel and his time with the watchers. It also gave us some insight to his POV from the first book on a few scenes and showed what else was going on at the same time adding even more dimension to the story and his character.<br /><br />World After is really a dark story. I was very worried about the characters at certain parts of the book when it became the darkest and pushed the envelope of even the first book. But Susan Ee really hits you with some levity throughout too. For it being about the apocalypse I really laughed quite a few times. Penryn and Raffe’s banter is fantastic once again.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>”Don’t talk. You’ll just spoil my fantasy of rescuing an innocent damsel in distress as soon as you open your mouth.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I was so happy when they found each other again and I might have fist bumped in the air. There is the forbidden romance and it is still smoldering and a slow burn. I ship these two so hard I really want it to work out for them in the end but an Angel and a Daughter of Man have a lot stacked against them it will be interesting to see how that progresses.<br /><br />The romance never overshadows the rest of the story and there is one dilemma after another. Questions are answered and others are posed but I feel like a good deal of the questions I had after the first book were at least addressed and I know so much more about this world and the motivations of all the characters than I did before.<br /><br />My new favorite character is……Pooky Bear. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Bow down to me Pooky Bear, who has only two other equals in all the worlds.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Until you read the book you won’t understand I just have to throw it in that it some of the funniest moments in the book and I laugh so hard just thinking about it. But don’t let the name fool you Pooky Bear kicks ass.<br /><br />I am wowed by this book it has action, adventure, sci-fi, monsters, A Crazy Mom, heroes, demons, Aerial Combat, crazy club scenes Gatsby Style, incredibly disturbing moments, incredibly hopeful moments and decidedly unexpected moments….there were a lot of moments. The ending left me aching for more. This is one of those books that I marked so many pages I loved it was hard to pick just a few things for the review. <br /><br />I really can’t wait to see what else pops out of the mind of Susan Ee. Well played Ms. Ee Well Played.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6435318142098010924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1870470096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1870470096" />
    <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood"><img alt="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596432515p2/50173624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1870470096?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood">Ashwood (애쉬 우드).</a>
      </span>

    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer718207219" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13139523576792643265"><b>*4.5 Stars!*<br/><br/>Absence really <i>does</i> make the heart grow fonder...</b><br/><br/>I <b>LOVED</b> this! I went into this sequel with some reserve, fairly unsure of what to expect, and I can honestly say that I fully enjoyed every moment of this suspenseful, action-packed, never predictable, twisted but just plain fun addition!<br/><br/><i>World After</i> picks up directly where <i>Angelfall</i> leaves off, at the peak of chaos and calamity. The story follows Penryn as she unknowingly becomes a warrior for her kind ... fighting for the survival of </span>
  <span id="freeText13139523576792643265" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars!*<br><br>Absence really <i>does</i> make the heart grow fonder...</b><br><br>I <b>LOVED</b> this! I went into this sequel with some reserve, fairly unsure of what to expect, and I can honestly say that I fully enjoyed every moment of this suspenseful, action-packed, never predictable, twisted but just plain fun addition!<br><br><i>World After</i> picks up directly where <i>Angelfall</i> leaves off, at the peak of chaos and calamity. The story follows Penryn as she unknowingly becomes a warrior for her kind ... fighting for the survival of herself, her family, and the innocent people surrounding her. The angels/demons have stepped up their "organized" plan of attack, but Penryn is intent on remaining one step ahead. Once again, she is the epitome of strength, intelligence, and perseverance — not to mention an official master at cracking hilarious <i>mental-mom</i> jokes. <br><br>This story offered just as much action as the last, but, due to Raffe's limited appearance, was lighter on the romance. However, none of it felt overdone or became tired. Yes, Raffe's now infamous prolonged absence was a bit of a hurdle, but it served well to build the anticipation. Plus, I found the story was strong enough to hold its own. I loved how the author cleverly inserted Raffe's POV without the use of dual perspectives. Allowing his sword to interact with Penryn kept Raffe's character present during his MIA moments. <br><br>But, at last, Raffe <i>does</i> return in the flesh, and we are once again united with all the humor, sexiness, witty banter, and fierce protection his amazing character exudes. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"Don't talk. You'll just spoil my fantasy of rescuing an innocent damsel in distress as soon as you open your mouth."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Susan Ee is just a fabulous storyteller. Not only is this storyline top notch and original, but its delivery is just as captivating. The scenes glide effortlessly into one another with words that feel light and smooth, yet paint a powerful picture. This sequel offers the perfect ratio of peril, humor, and romance, and ends with a strategically constructed cliffhanger that opens up more story while offering just enough temporary resolve to satisfy. Impatiently wait for MORE... <b>Awesome read!</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> Dystopian/Post Apocalyptic/Angels <br><b>▪	 Steam Caliber:</b> Clean<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Working on it<br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Angel/protective hero. Strong, kickass heroine. <br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Penryn takes on the evil and struggles to keep her family safe. Reunites with Raffe. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Engaging, intense, fluid.<br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person: Heroine<br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> Yes, but enough resolve.<br><b>▪	 Next Installment:</b> Follow up. <br><b>▪ HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Yes, as happy as a post-apocalyptic, demon infested world can get ;) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_252619335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252619335" />
    <a title="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads"><img alt="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356098123p2/5183631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252619335?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)" href="/user/show/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads">Judith (Judith&#39;sChoiceReads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=romance-for-the-win">romance-for-the-win</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=2013-releases">2013-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=crazy-romantic">crazy-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=heroines-with-spunk">heroines-with-spunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=crazy-phenomenal">crazy-phenomenal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=good-reads">good-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=hunks-of-the-world">hunks-of-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=series-i-love">series-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5183631-judith-judith-schoicereads?shelf=read-again">read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252619335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15435739370418441032"><br/>This book had better come out <b>ASAP</b> 2013. I need it now, like candy or Ian Somerhalder, and on second thought, perhaps even more. This one is going to be fantastic, no doubt about it! Hurry up, Ee, you officially rocked my socks, period.<br/><br/><br/><i>Update: January 3, 2014</i> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Review</u>
</b><br/><br/>There are no words for this book. The funny thing is that I went in expecting nothing but perfection. Ee floored me with <i>Angelfall</i> and I just couldn't conceive of a world where the book following such excellence was lacking in </span>
  <span id="freeText15435739370418441032" style="display:none"><br>This book had better come out <b>ASAP</b> 2013. I need it now, like candy or Ian Somerhalder, and on second thought, perhaps even more. This one is going to be fantastic, no doubt about it! Hurry up, Ee, you officially rocked my socks, period.<br><br><br><i>Update: January 3, 2014</i> <br><br><b>
  <u>My Review</u>
</b><br><br>There are no words for this book. The funny thing is that I went in expecting nothing but perfection. Ee floored me with <i>Angelfall</i> and I just couldn't conceive of a world where the book following such excellence was lacking in any way. I needed <i>World After</i> to be as good, if not better than <i>Angelfall</i>. Spoiler Alert: It was.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388788325ra/7930237.gif" width="340" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The curse of the second is pretty much something I implicate when going into sequels, simply said, they tend to be less enthralling than their predecessors. But the curse? It didn't exist for this book. Ee is an author after my own heart, this is why her books are my kryptonite, I feel like she writes <i>for</i> me. So thank-you for this, Ee, it was superb.<br><br><i>World After</i> follows the events of <i>Angelfall</i> and Penryn is slowly recovering from the scorpion sting that left her paralysed. She's with her family, Paige is finally returned, but the experimentations done on her have altered Penryn's baby sister in ways that go much deeper than the physical. Her pain was palpable, and finding the sister she lost in the "Low Demon" now in her stead was a struggle for Penryn. Her mother, craziness aside, latches onto her daughter and encourages Penryn to look in Paige's eyes because those haven't changed; she is the same sister and daughter they know and lost. Surprisingly, Penryn has difficulty with this, and if things aren't hard enough, they still don't know what to feed Paige. It isn't until one incident at their base refugee camp that the gory answer is arrived at.<br><br>Paige needs meat. Raw meat, most readily available in human beings. There is an uproar, and the rest of the survivors try to capture her and she flees the camp, leaving Penryn and her mother to find Paige yet again. Clara, an unexpected survivor who Penryn saves from being sucked dry by the scorpions/"locusts" comes along for the ride, and together they embark on the quest to save Paige from the unpredictable angels, herself, and from hurting anyone else. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388788325ra/7930238.gif" width="340" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Yeah, not so much.</i><br><br>I was taken rapture, by the incredible storytelling and the characters brimming with anguish and determination to survive. I think more than anything, this series is a chronicle of survival and persistence even at the worst of times. <br><br>Penryn grew, into the kind of Heroine one cannot forget about simply by closing the book. She stays with you, making you question her actions as well as what you might do in her place. If your world was turned upside down, the man you loved apart from you, and your family ravaged...what would you do? I'd hope I would act as Penryn did and kick some serious ass! Can I get a "what-what" for her skills with Pookie Bear!? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388788325ra/7930239.gif" width="340" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was very pleased, and excited that more of Raffe's past was revealed through his sword and also that some insight as to what Paige went through was provided. I think I would have hated it if her whole experience with the angels was glossed over, and Ee gave just enough detail about her abduction that satisfied but did not completely satiate my curiosity. As always, I am hungry for more and the next book is something I absolutely <i>must have</i>.<br><br><i>World After</i> was full of action and entertained me to the very end. Much is revealed about the Angels as well as their purpose on Earth. Uriah's motives are despicable, but then again was any less expected? Things are more complicated than they appear and I am glad there will be <b>5 books</b> to unravel the mystery of this new world and its many conspiracies.<br><br>Did I mention, I am hella pleased to have more Raffe and Penryn coming my way? I NEED this two to happen, damnation aside. Their chemistry is crackling and my tummy warmed at their reunion. I'm shipping this so hard, it hurts. Raffe did not disappoint me and the fact that he recognized Penryn right away made the romantic in me swoon for days! I'm in love. <i>World After</i> is the kind of book that satisfies and I am so happy.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380379134ra/734798.gif" width="340" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This book was everything I needed it to be, the perfect sequel with an ending that makes me ever loyal to Ee and this series. So beautifully written...All I want is the next book!</b><br><br><b>5 FLAMING STARS!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15435739370418441032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_373279653" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373279653" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373279653?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=extremely-unique">extremely-unique</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-other">paranormal-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=angels-nephilim-and-demons">angels-nephilim-and-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=action-and-adventure">action-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dystopia-or-apocalyptic">dystopia-or-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373279653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7282067529432037261"><b>A teenager, a mutated girl, a tattered angel, and a sword named Pooky Bear walk into a bar...</b><br/><br/>[insert punchline here]<br/><br/>[end result = win]<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b>. Spoilers for book 1 only. I promise that there are no major spoilers here for <i>World After</i>, but I am placing a couple of quotes in this review with the assumption that most readers would figure Penryn and Raffe were going to cross paths again at some point. I just won't say when or how.<br/><br/>Not that I wasn't already in love with this series, but when the swor</span>
  <span id="freeText7282067529432037261" style="display:none"><b>A teenager, a mutated girl, a tattered angel, and a sword named Pooky Bear walk into a bar...</b><br /><br />[insert punchline here]<br /><br />[end result = win]<br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b>. Spoilers for book 1 only. I promise that there are no major spoilers here for <i>World After</i>, but I am placing a couple of quotes in this review with the assumption that most readers would figure Penryn and Raffe were going to cross paths again at some point. I just won't say when or how.<br /><br />Not that I wasn't already in love with this series, but when the sword started interacting with Penryn, I did an internal happy dance. Who knows why I like swords with attitude, but I do.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I carefully pull out the bear and sword. I proudly flip the bridal veil skirt to show him the scabbard.<br /><br />Raffe stares at the disguised sword for a second before commenting. "Do you know how many kills this sword has?"<br /><br />"It's a perfect disguise, Raffe."<br /><br />"This sword is not just an angel sword. She's an archangel sword. Better than an angel sword, in case that's not clear. She intimidates other angel swords."<br /><br />"What, the other swords quake in their scabbards when they see her?"<br /><br />"Yes, if you must know," he says following me. "She was made for ultimate respect. How is she supposed to get that disguised as a teddy bear in a bridal gown?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I know a few people weren't fond of the pacing in this book, but I was pretty much happy with the entire thing. The dream sequences could have been pared back to one or two scenes, but since I liked the interaction between Penryn and Pooky Bear, I didn't mind the scenes either. It gave the reader some knowledge of what Raffe was thinking without having to add chapters in his PoV.<br /><br />The banter between Raffe and Penryn was great. One of the things that I appreciate the most about Raffe is that he is very focused and serious, but still has these moments of hilarity which break through.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You're not Fallen, are you?"<br /><br />"From everything I've heard, that would just make me more sexy to you Daughters of Men. What is it that you all see in bad boys?"<br /><br />.....<br /><br />"Oh, don't worry. You're safe," he says in a reassuring voice. "I'd never tell you that you have a nice personality."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />There are still an ample amount of action scenes, fight scenes, survival scenes, etc. for the people who crave all of that dark post-apocalyptic goodness. I thought the balance of action to sexual tension was perfect for what I like to read. Others might wish for less swooning, but I didn't mind having a few moments here and there to break up some of the science experiments and fight scenes.<br /><br />The side characters are still around and contributing to this crazy story. Both Paige and her mom were back to add a few bizarre scenes to the mix. When you have a whack-job fanatic and a razor-toothed little girl demon on the scene, things are bound to go a little nutty.<br /><br />Add in a creepy turn on Alcatraz and an epic angel battle, and we have a well-rounded story. The way things ended has me itching for book 3 and I know that I'll be re-reading <i>World After</i> in the meantime because it was that good. <br /><br />I have nothing else to say but <b>read this series!</b> <br /><br />My review can also be found on <a href="http://stacia.booklikes.com/post/706316/a-teenager-a-mutated-girl-a-tattered-angel-and-a-sword-named-pooky-bear-walk-into-a-bar-" rel="nofollow noopener">Booklikes</a><br /><br />Are you an adult who loves to read and chat about young adult books? Join us over in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/51118" rel="nofollow noopener">Rated YA-MA</a> group!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7282067529432037261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13761200521449560832">I loved this, I really did...just not as much as the first book.<br/>I think the reason has to do with the lack of Raffe for the majority of the time. He's off doing <i>stuff</i>, and Penryn is on her own trying to save the day.<br/>Which is cool. Really!<br/>I think the story was more entertaining when they were all bickery with each other.<br/><i>*shrugs*</i><br/><br/><i>

  <span id="freeText13761200521449560832" style="display:none">I loved this, I really did...just not as much as the first book.<br>I think the reason has to do with the lack of Raffe for the majority of the time. He's off doing <i>stuff</i>, and Penryn is on her own trying to save the day.<br>Which is cool. Really!<br>I think the story was more entertaining when they were all bickery with each other.<br><i>*shrugs*</i><br><br><i>
  <b>For those of you who don't like to know anything before you read a book, there are mild spoilers in this review. Be warned!</b>
</i><br><br><b>Ok, so what happens in this book?</b><br>Crazy-Mom gets <i>crazier</i>, because the nutty gleam in her eyes and rotten egg fetish weren't bad enough. She's like an insane ninja sneaking around and taking out perceived threats.<br>Still.<br><b>Insane</b> is the key word to remember here.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429033725ra/14519135.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <b>
  <i>What-Happened-To-Paige</i>
</b> mystery is delved into a lot deeper, and we find out that she may be suffering from Stockholm syndrome. <i>*cough*</i> Among other things.<br>Penryn has a hard time looking her little sister in the eyeballs, which causes some trust issues. Especially when villagers with the torches and pitchforks decide she ate a dude.<br>Did she?<br><i>Well, it's possible...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429033590ra/14519110.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Remember the Scorpion things that the angels were cooking up in those incubating vats?<br>Guess what? Soylent Green is people!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414847106ra/11698751.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, it looks like there's a HUGE <i>Apocalypse</i> conspiracy going on that most of the angels are unaware of, and Penryn has stepped right in the middle of it. I'm so crazy excited to see where exactly Susan Ee is going with this one! I have theories. Many theories.<br>One of them is bound to be right, I just know it...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416364441ra/11943815.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were plenty of other fun tidbits sprinkled throughout the book that made up (somewhat) for the lack of Raffe.<br>Such as:<br><b>Pookie Bear!</b> The most accessorized sword to be wielded by a <s>archangel</s> teenage girl...<br>And what kind of accessories does an ass-kickin' sword need, you ask?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429032857i/14518931._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, of course, we finally get an answer to the age old question: <b>Can angels swim?</b><br>Although, in the ocean, does it <i>really</i> matter?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413147157ra/11471423.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also reviewed for:<br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/04/review-world-after-penryn-end-of-days-2.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>

    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1245491139?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=teenie-bopper-books">teenie-bopper-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it">end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1245491139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2265363762279759400">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428332583ra/14407059.gif' alt='Dallas Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I decided to break my own rule of reading Book #2 in a series after finishing <i>Angelfall</i> last year and giving it 3.5 Stars (that’s like the equivalent of 7 Stars for most people). I’m giving <i>World After</i> a very generous 3 Stars in hopes that the soon-to-be-released Book #3 gets back on track.<br/><br/>The problem I have with YA books in a series is there always seems to be so much filler that should have been left on the cutting room floor. Wh</span>
  <span id="freeText2265363762279759400" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428332583ra/14407059.gif" alt="Dallas Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I decided to break my own rule of reading Book #2 in a series after finishing <i>Angelfall</i> last year and giving it 3.5 Stars (that’s like the equivalent of 7 Stars for most people). I’m giving <i>World After</i> a very generous 3 Stars in hopes that the soon-to-be-released Book #3 gets back on track.<br><br>The problem I have with YA books in a series is there always seems to be so much filler that should have been left on the cutting room floor. While <i>World After</i> contained a few awesome action sequences and answered some questions like “what the F are those scorpion pod things?!?!?!?!?!” and “how did little Paige end up a Frankenhuman?!?!?!?!?” there was <b>a lot</b> of time spent doing pretty much nothing. And when Penryn <b>was</b> doing stuff, it was kind of the same stuff she did in <i>Angelfall</i> - like infiltrating the angels’ new aerie. Not to mention that, although Penryn is way more kickass than the average YA female lead, a certain <i>someone</i> . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428332583ra/14407060.gif" alt="Dallas Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>didn’t even appear until the <b>72% point</b>. WTF? It’s great to have a heroine who can hold her own, but it’s even better with Raffe’s banter . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Don’t talk. You’ll just spoil my fantasy of rescuing an innocent damsel in distress as soon as you open your mouth.”</i>
</b><br><br>Crossing my fingers that <i>End of Days</i> has less of this . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428332583ra/14407061.gif" alt="Dallas Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and a lot more of this . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428332583ra/14407062.gif" alt="Dallas Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>or even this . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/dallas/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1282353434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282353434" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1282353434?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477817285" href="/book/show/18071466-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282353434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15332143638000556539"><b> 4 creepy stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/world%20after%20collage.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432002261i/14892393._SX540_.png' alt=' photo world after collage.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This book. Oh my god this book. I spent a part of it freaked out, another part grossed out and a third part of it I was heartwarmed. <b> How does Susan Ee do this? Is she a brilliant author mastermind? </b><br/><br/>I remember when this book was released I got it in the mail from amazon and I ripped open the package and started reading right away, because I had to know Raffe's reaction when he saw Penryn</span>
  <span id="freeText15332143638000556539" style="display:none"><b> 4 creepy stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/world%20after%20collage.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432002261i/14892393._SX540_.png" alt=" photo world after collage.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book. Oh my god this book. I spent a part of it freaked out, another part grossed out and a third part of it I was heartwarmed. <b> How does Susan Ee do this? Is she a brilliant author mastermind? </b><br><br>I remember when this book was released I got it in the mail from amazon and I ripped open the package and started reading right away, because I had to know Raffe's reaction when he saw Penryn again. But Raffe wasn't in the beginning. Then I started skimming and he wasn't in the middle. I kept flipping the pages and went to the ending and there he was! The last 20% or so of the book he appears. In a fit of rage I put the book down and didn't pick it up again until now. And I'm glad I waited, because it gave me time to appreciate what was happening at the beginning of the book in a way I know I wouldn't have appreciated (basically I would have skimmed). <br><br><b> World After </b> picks up directly after the ending of Angelfall. Penryn and her family are with the resistance and things are not going very well. Paige looks like a disturbing demon frankenstein baby and is having trouble keeping down food. Penryn's mother is as cray-cray as ever, and it's up to Penryn to keep them all alive (as per usual). <br><br><b> <i> “I’m fine, Mom. Thanks for asking."<br>“Of course you’re fine. You’re the devil’s bride and these are his creatures.”<br>“I’m not the devil’s bride.” <br>“He carried you out of the fire and is letting you visit us from the dead. Who else would have those privileges except his bride?” </i> </b><br><br>Soon catastrophe strikes and Paige is separated from her family again. Penryn, her mother and a woman named Clara all leave the resistance together to go find her, and find up becoming trapped on the island of Alcatraz.<br><br>This book was captivating, even if at times the descriptions made me feel sick. The new world that was created after the angel strike is such a harsh and sinister one, survival of the fittest and every man for himself. I was particularly creeped out by the scorpion creatures, how they were made and what they ate. Yuck. <br><br>I was surprised by how much of the book I enjoyed without Raffe, Penryn on her own just showed the reader how strong and determined she is, how she'll do anything to save her younger sister even if she is a little bit frightened of her. It was also a compelling glimpse at what humanity looks like when put in extreme conditions together.<br><br>Overall a great middle book for a trilogy, but it was a little too dark and twisted for me to give it a full five stars. But that's just personal preference.<br><br><b> <i> “You're naming your collector's-item, kick-ass sword that's made to maim and kill, specifically designed to bring your ginormous enemies to their knees and hear the lamentation of their women-Pooky Bear?"<br>"Yeah, you like it?” </i> </b> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15332143638000556539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anja H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h"><img alt="Anja H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559051853p2/6054186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608996681?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608996681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2891553749371208447"><b>*5 APOCALYPTIC STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"It is painful to see that people prefer a bad guy who looks like an angel to a good guy who looks like a demon.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Yes, yeesss, <b>YEESSSSS</b>! Someone pinch me because this was just too perfect!<br/>I think I loved this novel even more than the previous one! Yes, even though Penryn and Raffe were apart for the better part of this. Their reunion made it all worth it though!<br/><br/>I felt like them being apart for a while, made them develop more as individual characters and it made me love th</span>
  <span id="freeText2891553749371208447" style="display:none"><b>*5 APOCALYPTIC STARS*</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"It is painful to see that people prefer a bad guy who looks like an angel to a good guy who looks like a demon.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Yes, yeesss, <b>YEESSSSS</b>! Someone pinch me because this was just too perfect!<br />I think I loved this novel even more than the previous one! Yes, even though Penryn and Raffe were apart for the better part of this. Their reunion made it all worth it though!<br /><br />I felt like them being apart for a while, made them develop more as individual characters and it made me love them even more than I already did, if that's even possible. Also, don't get me started on <i>Pooky Bear</i>! Some of the scenes involving Pooky Bear made me laugh out loud so hard that my boyfriend lying next to me started thinking I'd gone crazy lol.<br /><br />These books were so damn good that I'm only writing this review now, now that I've already read the entire trilogy. I just didn't want to miss a single second by writing reviews and after finishing one book, I immediately dived into the next. (sorry for that haha, I'll be writing all my missing reviews soon!)<br /><br />I advise everyone who hasn't read these books yet, to pick them up <b>asap</b>, they're definitely worth it and you won't be disappointed! I did notice that not each and every review of these books is as raving as mine, but I think it's mainly the characters that drew me in, as well as the entire setting. Penryn, Raffe <s>(and Pooky Bear)</s> are all great in their own way and they just have everything I'm always looking for in a main character. Suspense is also something really important in a book for me, and you can't deny that these books have a lot of that as well!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_646168377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646168377" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646168377?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12983100-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=awesome-kickass-heroines">awesome-kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646168377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10499274083161630811">Let me be honest with you, friends - my experience with Young Adult novels, those featuring either postapocalyptic or dystopian themes, and those with any hints of paranormal romances, has been mostly, well, uninspiring, to say the least. But yet I keep digging through the piles of dreck, forgetting the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/quotes/5543-insanity-is-doing-the-same-thing-over-and-over-again' rel='nofollow noopener'>famous misattributed Einstein's definition of insanity</a>, because among the piles of manure there may occasionally be a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328662528' rel='nofollow noopener'>gem</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134038899' rel='nofollow noopener'>two</a>.<br/><br/>Susan Ee's debut novel, <i>Angelfall</i>, pleasantly surprised me, fallin</span>
  <span id="freeText10499274083161630811" style="display:none">Let me be honest with you, friends - my experience with Young Adult novels, those featuring either postapocalyptic or dystopian themes, and those with any hints of paranormal romances, has been mostly, well, uninspiring, to say the least. But yet I keep digging through the piles of dreck, forgetting the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/quotes/5543-insanity-is-doing-the-same-thing-over-and-over-again" rel="nofollow noopener">famous misattributed Einstein's definition of insanity</a>, because among the piles of manure there may occasionally be a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328662528" rel="nofollow noopener">gem</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134038899" rel="nofollow noopener">two</a>.<br><br>Susan Ee's debut novel, <i>Angelfall</i>, pleasantly surprised me, falling in with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349806416" rel="nofollow noopener">the gems, not the manure</a>. It was a surprisingly refreshing read, earning very positive responses from the audience. <i>World After</i> is a much-anticipated sequel to the promising first volume, and overall it did not disappoint me, earning a solid 3.5 star rating - a very decent grade for a middle book in the series as far as I'm concerned. <b>Was it perfect or at least as good as it's predecessor? Well, no - but for all it's flaws it had enough redeeming qualities and, just like the first book, kept my full undivided rapt attention for its entire 300+ pages.</b><br><br>The first book introduced us to the life in California's Silicon Valley a couple of months after an invasion by none other than angels, who turned out to be a brutal thuggish force and left cities in ruins and those few of the humans not yet decimated desperately looking for ways to survive - ranging from prostituting themselves to forming the Resistance. <br><br>Enter Penryn Young, a teenage girl whose experience with studying martial arts for years comes in handy in the world in which she needs to fend for her paranoid schizophrenic mother and paraplegic younger sister against both humans and angels, each group equally dangerous. Penryn teams up with a newly wingless angel Raffe (<i>how long did it take you to assume that cocky Adonis-like [barf!!!] Raffe = legendary Rafael? It took me about 2 paragraphs. Can you beat me?</i>) . <b>One decadent Gatsby-style angelic party, mutant scorpions and reengineered children, and a pair of demon wings later - and we arrive at the events of <i>World After</i>, again full of angelic parties and mutant scorpions.</b><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387569086i/7622059._SX540_.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Ahh, Scorpions... I just couldn't resist even though I realize I'm really dating myself with this reference. <a href="http://m.youtube.com/watch?v=n4RjJKxsamQ" rel="nofollow noopener">"Wind of Change"</a>was so idealistically popular when I was a child, and the sound of it still makes me want to wave a lighter in a slow-mo to the haunting music.</i> Taaaaake me to the magic of the moment on a gloooory night where the children of tomorrow dream awaaaaay in the wind of change.....</blockquote><br>Ahem, anyway, back to this book.<br><br><i>World After</i> gives us more of the same, really, expanding a bit on what was already shown. There's a bit more of politics, experiments leading to creation of mutants, cruelty from the invaders and the Resistance alike. Penryn's mother gets a bit more character development, which is quite welcome. Little Paige has become something entirely else than human, and is turning into something more than simply a plot-advancing McGuffin she was starting to become in the first book. And her story is quite sad, but just as your heartstrings feel tugged on a bit too much, an unexpected bloodshed or two will surely fix the mood.<br><br>As for Penryn herself - she is still a great heroine. She finds a few more occasions to demonstrate her fighting skills, and holds her own against a variety of opponents. There's a bit of sarcastic humor in her that feels genuine even if occasionally too juvenile (Pooky Bear, anyone?). <b>To her credit, she remains resourceful and practical, and kicks ass, even if some scenes are full of quite forced stereotypical <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/WaifFu" rel="nofollow noopener">waif-fu </a></b><i>(seriously, learning sword fighting via dream sequences makes me cringe. Good thing it's a magical super-duper special sword that can pretty much wield itself).</i> While very much acting age-appropriately for a teenager, she mostly avoids the annoying stereotypes that plague countless similar books.<br><br>As for the worldbuilding, Susan Ee does not shy away from unpleasantness, either. She adds just the necessary touch of gore and gritty to add some weight and consequences to her world. She knows when to to switch the pace of her narration with a well-placed action scene or two.<br><br>And even when at the end of this book you do realize that the storyline has not advanced all that much despite all the action, you still can't help but overall enjoy the experience.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387569776i/7622246._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Well, that was the good. Now let's take a peek at the bad and the ugly. </u><br><br>All of the above, while sometimes too juvenile and too naive, was still fun to read about, and written quite decently at that. <b>The parts that were losing me, however, had to do with the Adonis-like love interest, the one and only Raffe. </b>Supposedly an ancient archangel, he does play a part of hormonal teenager convincingly, actually too convincingly for it to be enjoyable. <br><br>Book writers, listen up. You want to have an ancient creature in love with your teenage protagonist? Fine; I don't quite get the appeal of such a pairing but what do I know? You want to have a witty banter of two hormonal teenagers? Fine. You want to combine the two ideas above? Fine as long as you're aware that your ancient creature acting like a sixteen-year-old is, quite honestly, creepily disturbing. Please have Penryn's love interest be either Rafael, the respected archangel or Raffe, the cocky young kid - but the amalgam of above is dysfunctional.<br><br><b>Also: nonstop witty banter, even in the middle of a battle, cute as it may be, can get juuuust a bit tiring and eventually annoying.</b> It has time and place, and it's okay to let the gravity of the situation stand without punctuating it with lighthearted fun banter. It lessens the emotional impact and wears thin after a while. Oh, and the witty bantering adorable teenage twin brothers? Other than Fred and George Weasley, few can pull it off without becoming silly comedic relief - and the twin duo in this story, sadly, is not up to par.<br>----------------------<br><b>When weighing the good and the bad in this book, the scale still tips towards the positive for me.</b> Despite the flaws and the annoyances, it is still overall an interesting and decent read that retains quite a bit of the appeal of the first story and remains full of promise for the remaining books in the series. Whether the rest of the story lives up to the promise or succumbs to the flaws that are so common in this genre - well, only time will tell. But I surely will be reading the next book in the series. <br><b>3.5 stars.</b><br>----------------------<br>My review of <i>Angelfall</i>, the first book in this series, is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349806416" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10499274083161630811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1704831014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1704831014" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1704831014?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477817285" href="/book/show/18071466-world-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1704831014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17052618894176331429"><b>"It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive."</b><br/><br/>•My mind took its sweet time to put its finger (mine? Whatever) on the reason why I wasn't enjoying <i>World After</i> the same way I'd enjoyed <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a>.</i> At last, I realized that the main problem was very simple: <b>the plot is too similar to that of the previous book</b>. <br/>Desperate initial situation. Baby sister is missing. Let's go look for her. Insert in the middle three or four attacks and sundry misadventures so that t</span>
  <span id="freeText17052618894176331429" style="display:none"><b>"It’s amazing how many times we need to go against our survival instincts to survive."</b><br /><br />•My mind took its sweet time to put its finger (mine? Whatever) on the reason why I wasn't enjoying <i>World After</i> the same way I'd enjoyed <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>.</i> At last, I realized that the main problem was very simple: <b>the plot is too similar to that of the previous book</b>. <br />Desperate initial situation. Baby sister is missing. Let's go look for her. Insert in the middle three or four attacks and sundry misadventures so that the pace is balanced, then take a nap until crazy Mom calls you for dinner. Which may never happen, come that I think of it.<br />In this respect, <b>I expected something</b>, let alone original, but at least<b> new</b>, <b>not certainly a cut-and-paste</b>.<br /><br />•<b>Why do the chapters last, on average, four pages</b>? Of course it's not a flaw in itself and I can't remember if the same happened in <i>Angelfall</i> (if it did, I didn't notice at all), but when a dram that could easily occupy just one chapter of eight pages at most gets to occupy two super-short chapters for no reason, that does seem strange.<b> It compromises the fluidity</b> of the whole narrative, in my opinion.<br /><br />•I guess it's due to the fact that the different specifics of the single situations no longer offer the best suitable circumstances for <b>Penryn</b> to show those parts of her personality that had captivated me so much, but I found her<b> slightly less impressive</b> than in the first installment. She still remains absolutely likeable and relatable, though, and I challenge anyone to do better in her position (and with a Mom like hers in tow).<br /><br />•Speaking about this, <b>Penryn's family</b> very likely is one of the things that make this series absolutely <b>unique</b>. Her mom is a total psycho and her sister is a man-eating little monster (plus other things), which just adds to the general <b>delicious creepiness</b> of the atmosphere. Respects.<br /><br />•I'm not including this in the reasons why I think the first book is superior, because this was just how the story had to unfold and again, not a flaw in itself, but <b>Raffe barely appears</b>. Just thought I should warn you.<br /><br />➽ Accurate diagnostic tests resulted in the identification of <b>a relatively serious middle-book syndrome</b>. Any recommendation would be pretty useless since the conclusion to the series has already been written and published, therefore, let's just hope for the better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17052618894176331429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_25820414'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25820414-rhapsodic"><img alt="Rhapsodic (The Bargainer, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1466107203l/25820414._SX98_SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I6E+J5zOd3lWG1vzAd9sx449pSeyvo4KgFFgK61k3tgZh1f1J5C+EfEw75L2KmYYWGJC73wzAG3bLyaaYCcsQg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0oonzPjghgiXD64r60+yOVph4SJUOPNdU0BPQX/LH0HorE4eQ75PYDAkGkocurjmjD4G6pq1fToIPgnwsojt2w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
